Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Obstructive sleep apnea (OSA) is caused by the repetitive collapse of the upper airway during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor of odontogenic epithelium.
  Dentigerous cyst is a developmental odontogenic cyst associated with the crown of an unerupted tooth.
  Orbital fracture is a break in one or more bones surrounding the eye.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition in which the mandibular condyle is fused to the temporal bone.
  None of the options seem to be related to the causes of OSA.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition where a person's breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep.
  TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint is stiff and movement is restricted.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can cause airway obstruction and lead to obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a type of jaw tumor that can cause swelling and pain but is not known to cause sleep apnoea.
  Dentigerous cyst is a type of jaw cyst that can cause swelling and pain but is not known to cause sleep apnoea.
  Orbital fracture is a fracture of the bones surrounding the eye and is not known to cause sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

  The answer is C: 5 in each quadrant.

Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has a history of myocardial infarction.
  The lipid profile reveals low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels.
  The patient should be prescribed a lipid-lowering therapy.
  Statins are the first-line therapy for lipid-lowering.
  Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are both statins.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative and can be used in combination with statins.
  However, the combination of Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate is not preferred due to the increased risk of adverse effects.
  Therefore, the preferred option for this patient would be a statin alone.
  The correct option is C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The patient has a history of myocardial infarction, which means he has a high risk of cardiovascular disease.
  The lipid profile shows high triglycerides (TG) and low high-density lipoprotein (HDL) levels, which are both risk factors for cardiovascular disease.
  The low-density lipoprotein (LDL) level is also high, which is another risk factor for cardiovascular disease.
  The preferred treatment for this patient would be a medication that can lower LDL levels and either raise HDL levels or lower TG levels.
  Option A combines Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate, which can lower LDL levels and TG levels and raise HDL levels.
  Option B only includes Fenofibrate, which can lower TG levels but may not be as effective in reducing LDL levels.
  Option C only includes Rosuvastatin, which can lower LDL levels but may not be as effective in raising HDL levels or lowering TG levels.
  Option D includes a high dose of Atorvastatin, which can lower LDL levels but may not be as effective in raising HDL levels or lowering TG levels.
  Therefore, the best option for this patient would be A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:

  The lipid profile reveals low HDL, high LDL, and very high TG levels.
  Statins are the first-line therapy for high LDL cholesterol.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that can lower TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  Combination therapy with statins and fibrates may increase the risk of myopathy and rhabdomyolysis.
  Therefore, the preferred therapy for this patient is statin therapy alone.
  Among the given choices, options A, B, and D include fenofibrate, which is not the preferred therapy for this patient.
  Option C includes only rosuvastatin 10 mg, which is a reasonable dose for this patient.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is a narrow cavity filled with cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) in the midline of the brain.
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus and the optic chiasm.
  The optic stalk is a structure that connects the developing eye to the brain.
  The third nerve is a cranial nerve that originates in the midbrain and controls eye movement.
  The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland.
  The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is the mammillary body.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
The floor of the third ventricle is formed by a number of structures including the optic chiasm, the infundibulum, the mammillary bodies, and the cerebral peduncles. 
The third nerve (oculomotor nerve) is not located on the floor of the third ventricle.
Therefore, the answer is B: Third nerve.

Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine.
  It is used to protect against pneumococcal disease, which is caused by bacteria called Streptococcus pneumoniae.
  Cystic fibrosis patients and sickle cell anemia patients are at higher risk of pneumococcal disease as their immune system is compromised.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may also benefit from PPV-23 as they are more susceptible to pneumococcal infections.
  Children less than 2 years of age are usually vaccinated with PCV-13 (pneumococcal conjugate vaccine) as they are at higher risk of pneumococcal infections.
  Therefore, the patient who is most beneficial for PPV-23 is either A, B, or C.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine.
  It is used to prevent infections caused by the Streptococcus pneumoniae bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis and sickle cell anemia are not directly related to increased risk of Streptococcus pneumoniae infections.
  Recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may be caused by Streptococcus pneumoniae, but the vaccine may not be the most beneficial for this condition.
  Children less than 2 years of age are at increased risk of Streptococcus pneumoniae infections.
  Therefore, PPV-23 is most beneficial for children less than 2 years of age.

  If TSH is raised in the presence of low T4, it suggests primary hypothyroidism.
  If TSH is raised in the presence of normal or raised T4, it suggests secondary hypothyroidism.
  Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is a TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
  The answer is C: TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure that involves the removal of the entire pulp from the tooth, followed by filling the root canals with a suitable material.
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure in which the exposed pulp is covered with a dressing or cement to protect the pulp from further injury and to promote healing and repair.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that develop in humans.
  Primary teeth are smaller in size and have a wider pulp chamber than permanent teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity in the young is the main reason for the success of pulpectomy and pulp capping in primary teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy is the removal of the entire pulp from the crown and root of a tooth followed by filling of the canal with a suitable material.
  Pulp capping is a technique used in dental restorations to prevent the dental pulp from dying, after being exposed, or nearly exposed during a cavity preparation.
  Primary teeth are also known as baby teeth and are replaced by permanent teeth.
  Primary teeth have wider pulp canals than permanent teeth.
  Pulp in primary teeth is more vascular and cellular than in permanent teeth.
  Increased vascularity and cellular activity of pulp in primary teeth make pulpectomy and pulp capping more successful.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex.
Action: Answer("B")

Among the given choices, +85 mV is the closest to the normal value of the endo-cochlear potential.
Therefore, the answer is D: +85 mV.

  The roots of the tooth have been denuded for 6 years, meaning the tooth has been exposed without any gingival tissue covering it.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres are fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  PDL fibres are attached to the cementum and alveolar bone, but not to the dentin.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the tooth and adjacent gingival tissue.
  Co-adaptation refers to the adaptation of the gingival tissue to the tooth surface.
  Therefore, in a lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibres will be attached to cementum, not dentin, and there will likely be epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.

  Therefore, chylomicrons have the least density.

Question: Digoxin is obtained from a plant product and has a half-life of 36 hours. How does this information help us in formulating treatment?
Choices:
  A: To adjust maintenance dose of digoxin required to keep the blood levels within therapeutic range
  B: Intravenous administration in emergency and urgent dosing
  C: Long half-life permits altemate day dosing
  D: It requires a high loading dose to be administered
Response 0:
Thought:
  Digoxin has a long half-life of 36 hours.
  A long half-life allows for a drug to remain in the body for a longer period of time.
  This information can be used to adjust the maintenance dose of digoxin required to keep the blood levels within therapeutic range.
  Therefore, the answer is A: To adjust maintenance dose of digoxin required to keep the blood levels within therapeutic range.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Half-life is the time it takes for half of the drug to be eliminated from the body.
  Digoxin has a long half-life of 36 hours.
  A long half-life permits less frequent dosing.

  Defective occlusal balancing means that the RPD is not fitting properly on the occlusal surface of the teeth.
  Passive clasp on abutment means that the clasp is not fitting properly on the abutment tooth.
  Thin flange means that the flange area of the RPD is not thick enough.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth means that the RPD does not have enough overlapping on the posterior teeth.
  Out of these, the most likely cause of looseness in an RPD is a passive clasp on abutment.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Passive clasp on abutment.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: Which of the following may be a feature of acromegaty?
Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a disorder that results from excess growth hormone (GH) after the growth plates have closed.
  The excess GH stimulates the liver to produce insulin-like growth factor-1 (IGF-1) which leads to overgrowth of bones and soft tissues.
  The overgrowth of bones may cause changes in facial features, hands, and feet.
  A large tongue is a feature of acromegaly.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized and is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Crowded teeth may be a feature of acromegaly due to the overgrowth of the jaw.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Large tongue.

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Proteinuria is the presence of excess protein in the urine and is a sign of kidney damage.
  Severe preeclampsia is diagnosed when blood pressure is greater than 160/110 mm Hg and proteinuria is greater than or equal to 5 grams in a 24-hour urine sample or 3+ or greater on two random urine samples collected at least 4 hours apart.
  Therefore, the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is greater than or equal to 5 grams in a 24-hour urine sample.
  The answer is None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  According to the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists (ACOG), proteinuria of 5 grams or more in a 24-hour urine collection or a protein/creatinine ratio of 0.3 or more is consistent with severe preeclampsia.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 3000 mg.

  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lytic lesion on the midshaft of tibia in a 9-year-old boy.
  HPE shows grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm, and fibroblastic proliferation.
  The X-ray shows a lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion of the bone.
  The presentation is suggestive of a benign tumor.
  The most common benign tumor of the bone in this age group is osteoid osteoma.
  However, osteoid osteoma is usually smaller in size and presents with nocturnal pain that is relieved by aspirin.
  Giant cell tumor can also present with similar features but is less common in this age group.
  Chondroblastoma can also present with lytic lesion but is usually located in the epiphysis.
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis can present with lytic lesions and eosinophilic granuloma is the most common type found in the bone, but it is usually seen in younger children.
  Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is B: Giant cell tumor.

Topic: Dental
Question: Semi colon shaped C shaped canal is classified as (according to Melton and Seitzor)
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  The Melton and Seitz classification system is used to classify C-shaped canals.
  A C-shaped canal is defined as a canal that has a groove or a fin connecting the main canal to the pulp chamber.
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal has a groove that is shaped like a semi-colon.
  According to the Melton and Seitz classification system, a semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is classified as Type 3.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Type 3.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  According to Melton and Seitzor, there are four classifications of C-shaped canals.
  A C-shaped canal is a root canal with an oval or circular shape.
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is a type of C-shaped canal.
  Therefore, we need to identify which type of C-shaped canal a semi-colon shaped canal belongs to.
  Type 1 C-shaped canal has a single, continuous canal.
  Type 2 C-shaped canal has two separate canals that join at the apex.
  Type 3 C-shaped canal has three or more separate canals.
  Type 4 C-shaped canal has multiple canals that merge into one.
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is not a single, continuous canal (Type 1).
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is not two separate canals that join at the apex (Type 2).
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is not three or more separate canals (Type 3).
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is multiple canals that merge into one, which is Type 4.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought:
  The classification of the canal shape is based on the configuration of the canal.

  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Drugs taken by lactating mothers can be secreted in the milk and can affect the baby.
  The amount of drug that enters the milk depends on several factors, including the drug's chemical properties, the mother's dose, and the baby's age.
  Many drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk, but some can have adverse effects on the baby.
  Taking drugs with longer half-life can increase the amount of drug that enters the milk.
  Telling the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose can reduce the amount of drug that enters the milk.
  Telling the mother not to feed the baby if she is consuming any drug is not a good option as it can cause malnutrition and other problems for the baby.
  Therefore, the best advice would be to tell the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose.
  The answer is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.

Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is a series of enzymatic reactions that produce heme, a component of hemoglobin.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes in this pathway.
  The accumulation of which substance in blood reflects this inhibition?
  Uroporphyrinogen III and coproporphyrinogen III are intermediates in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Ferrochelatase is the enzyme that catalyzes the final step in the pathway.
  Delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA) and porphobilinogen (PBG) are precursors to porphyrins.
  The accumulation of which substance is most likely to reflect inhibition of the pathway?
  Delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA) is the precursor to porphobilinogen (PBG).
  ALA accumulates in blood and urine in lead poisoning.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.

Choices:
  A: Hypertonic Lower Lip
  B: Hypotonic Lower lip
  C: Hypertonic upper Lip
  D: Hypotonic upper lip
Response 0:

  Class II division 1 malocclusion is a dental classification.
  It is characterized by an overjet, which means the upper front teeth are positioned too far forward relative to the lower front teeth.
  Hypertonicity refers to excessive tension or contraction of the muscles.
  Hypotonicity refers to a lack of tension or contraction of the muscles.
  The lower lip is affected by the position of the lower front teeth.
  Therefore, patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have a Hypertonic Lower Lip.

Question: Which of the following is carcinoma of the skin, spreads by local invasion and has no tendency to metastasise?
Choices:
  A: Malignant melanoma
  B: Basal cell carcinoma
  C: Fibrosarcoma
  D: Leukoplakia
Response 0:
Thought:
  Carcinoma is a type of cancer that begins in the cells that line or cover an organ.
  The skin has three types of cells: basal cells, squamous cells, and melanocytes.
  Basal cell carcinoma is the most common type of skin cancer.
  It grows slowly and rarely spreads to other parts of the body.
  Malignant melanoma, on the other hand, is a more dangerous type of skin cancer that can spread quickly to other parts of the body.
  Fibrosarcoma is a type of cancer that begins in the fibrous tissue of the body.
  Leukoplakia is a condition in which thick, white patches form on the tongue and inside of the cheek.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Basal cell carcinoma.

Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
- Systematic random sampling is a technique in which every nth person is selected from a list.
- Simple random sampling is a technique where every member of the population has an equal chance of being selected.
- Stratified random sampling is a technique where the population is divided into subgroups and a random sample is selected from each subgroup.
- Cluster sampling is a technique where the population is divided into clusters and a random sample of clusters is selected for analysis.
- The question is asking about selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
- Stratified random sampling is used when subgroups have different characteristics and these characteristics may affect the results.
- Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:

  Stratified random sampling is a method for selecting a sample from a population where the population is divided into strata based on specific characteristics and then a random sample is taken from each stratum.
  Cluster sampling is a method for selecting a sample from a population where the population is divided into clusters and then a random sample of clusters is selected and all members of the selected clusters are included in the sample.
  The question is asking for a method for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.

Choices:

  B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days
  C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy
  D: No fuher action is necessary

  In cases of unprovoked dog bites, it is important to take immediate action to prevent rabies.
  The appropriate action is to give a vaccine.
  The vaccine should be given as soon as possible after the bite, ideally within 24 hours.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Give cell culture derived vaccine.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Dog bites can transmit rabies, a deadly viral disease.
  The virus is present in the saliva of infected animals and can be transmitted through bites.
  Post-exposure prophylaxis (PEP) should be initiated as soon as possible after an exposure to rabies.
  PEP consists of wound care, administration of rabies immunoglobulin (RIG), and rabies vaccine.
  In the case of an unprovoked dog bite, the dog should be observed for 10 days to see if it develops any symptoms of rabies.
  If the dog remains healthy after 10 days, the risk of rabies transmission is low.
  Therefore, the appropriate action in this case is to give cell culture-derived vaccine as soon as possible, along with wound care and administration of RIG.

  B: Class I type I
  C: Class II div I
  D: Class II div II

  Familial inheritance refers to the genetic transmission of traits from parents to offspring.
  In dentistry, malocclusion is the misalignment or incorrect relation between the teeth of the two dental arches when they approach each other as the jaws close.
  The Angle's classification of malocclusion is commonly used to describe the relationship between the maxillary and mandibular dental arches.
  Class I, Class II, and Class III are the three types of malocclusion in the Angle's classification.
  Class II is characterized by a retruded mandible and is further divided into Class II div I and Class II div II.
  Familial inheritance is a common feature of Class II div I malocclusion.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Class II div I.
